## Chapter: Understanding Urbanization and Development in Past and Present



### Introduction:



Urbanization and development have been two of the most significant processes shaping the world we live in today. The rapid growth of cities and the accompanying economic, social, and political changes have transformed societies and landscapes across the globe. As we continue to witness the ongoing urbanization and development of cities, it is crucial to understand the factors that have contributed to this phenomenon and the implications it has for local governance.



In this chapter, we will explore the structure and agency in local governance of developing cities. We will examine the various actors and institutions involved in governing these cities and how they interact to shape the development and growth of urban areas. We will also discuss the challenges and opportunities that arise in governing developing cities and the strategies that have been implemented to address them.



Through a historical and comparative lens, we will analyze the evolution of local governance in developing cities and how it has influenced urbanization and development. We will also explore the role of international organizations and policies in shaping the governance of these cities and their impact on urbanization and development.



Overall, this chapter aims to provide a comprehensive understanding of the complex relationship between urbanization, development, and local governance in developing cities. By examining the structure and agency in local governance, we can gain insights into the processes and dynamics that have shaped the urban landscape and continue to do so in the present day. 





### Section: 11.1 Governance Models and Structures in Developing Cities:



Governance is a crucial aspect of urbanization and development in developing cities. It is the process of making and enforcing decisions within an organization or society, and it plays a significant role in shaping the growth and development of cities. In this section, we will explore the various governance models and structures that exist in developing cities and their impact on urbanization and development.



#### 11.1a Definition of Governance



Governance can be defined as the process of interactions through laws, social norms, power, or language within an organized society. It involves decision-making and enforcement of rules and guidelines by various governing bodies, such as governments, organizations, and socio-political groups. The degree of formality in governance depends on the internal rules of a given social entity and its external business terms.



In the context of developing cities, governance is crucial in managing the rapid urbanization and development that these cities experience. It involves the coordination and collaboration of various actors and institutions to address the challenges and opportunities that arise in governing these cities. The goal of governance in developing cities is to create, reinforce, or reproduce acceptable conduct and social order while promoting the public good.



Governance in developing cities is a complex and dynamic process that is influenced by various factors, including historical, political, economic, and social contexts. It is essential to understand the different governance models and structures that exist in these cities to gain insights into the processes and dynamics that shape urbanization and development.



One of the most common governance models in developing cities is the government-led model, where the government has the sole responsibility and authority to make binding decisions. This model is often seen in authoritarian regimes, where the government has a significant influence on urbanization and development. In contrast, in democratic countries, the government operates as a democracy, and citizens have a say in decision-making processes.



Apart from government-led models, there are also other forms of governance in developing cities, such as market-led and network-led models. In market-led models, the market plays a significant role in decision-making and shaping urbanization and development. This model is often seen in capitalist economies, where the market forces drive development and growth.



In network-led models, decision-making is decentralized, and various actors and institutions collaborate to govern the city. This model is often seen in developing cities where there is a lack of strong central government and a need for community-based governance. It allows for more flexibility and adaptability in addressing the unique challenges and opportunities in these cities.



The choice of governance model in developing cities is influenced by various factors, including historical, political, and economic contexts. For instance, in countries with a history of colonialism, the government-led model may be more prevalent due to the legacy of centralized power. In contrast, in countries with a history of community-based governance, the network-led model may be more prevalent.



In conclusion, governance is a crucial aspect of urbanization and development in developing cities. It involves the coordination and collaboration of various actors and institutions to address the challenges and opportunities that arise in governing these cities. The choice of governance model is influenced by various factors, and understanding these models and structures is essential in gaining insights into the processes and dynamics that shape urbanization and development. 





### Section: 11.1 Governance Models and Structures in Developing Cities:



Governance plays a crucial role in the urbanization and development of cities, especially in developing cities where rapid growth and change are occurring. In this section, we will explore the various governance models and structures that exist in developing cities and their impact on urbanization and development.



#### 11.1a Definition of Governance



Governance can be defined as the process of making and enforcing decisions within an organization or society. It involves the coordination and collaboration of various actors and institutions to address the challenges and opportunities that arise in governing a city. In the context of developing cities, governance is crucial in managing the rapid urbanization and development that these cities experience.



Governance in developing cities is a complex and dynamic process that is influenced by various factors, including historical, political, economic, and social contexts. It is essential to understand the different governance models and structures that exist in these cities to gain insights into the processes and dynamics that shape urbanization and development.



One of the most common governance models in developing cities is the government-led model, where the government has the sole responsibility and authority to make binding decisions. This model is often seen in authoritarian regimes, where the government has a strong grip on power and controls most aspects of city development. In this model, decisions are made top-down, with little input from citizens or other stakeholders.



Another governance model that is prevalent in developing cities is the participatory model, where citizens and other stakeholders are actively involved in decision-making processes. This model promotes transparency and inclusivity, as it allows for the voices of different groups to be heard and considered in the decision-making process. However, this model can also be challenging to implement in developing cities, where there may be limited resources and capacity for citizen participation.



In addition to these models, there are also hybrid models of governance that combine elements of both government-led and participatory models. These models aim to strike a balance between top-down decision-making and citizen involvement, and they are often seen in cities that are transitioning from authoritarian regimes to more democratic systems.



The structure of governance in developing cities also plays a significant role in shaping urbanization and development. In some cities, there may be a centralized structure, where decision-making power is concentrated in a single governing body. This structure can lead to more efficient decision-making, but it may also limit the representation of diverse voices and perspectives.



On the other hand, some developing cities may have a decentralized governance structure, where decision-making power is distributed among multiple governing bodies. This structure allows for more local input and decision-making, but it can also lead to conflicts and inefficiencies if there is a lack of coordination among the different bodies.



In conclusion, governance models and structures in developing cities have a significant impact on urbanization and development. It is essential for city leaders and policymakers to understand these models and structures and their implications to effectively govern and manage the growth and development of their cities. 





### Section: 11.1 Governance Models and Structures in Developing Cities:



Governance plays a crucial role in the urbanization and development of cities, especially in developing cities where rapid growth and change are occurring. In this section, we will explore the various governance models and structures that exist in developing cities and their impact on urbanization and development.



#### 11.1a Definition of Governance



Governance can be defined as the process of making and enforcing decisions within an organization or society. It involves the coordination and collaboration of various actors and institutions to address the challenges and opportunities that arise in governing a city. In the context of developing cities, governance is crucial in managing the rapid urbanization and development that these cities experience.



Governance in developing cities is a complex and dynamic process that is influenced by various factors, including historical, political, economic, and social contexts. It is essential to understand the different governance models and structures that exist in these cities to gain insights into the processes and dynamics that shape urbanization and development.



One of the most common governance models in developing cities is the government-led model, where the government has the sole responsibility and authority to make binding decisions. This model is often seen in authoritarian regimes, where the government has a strong grip on power and controls most aspects of city development. In this model, decisions are made top-down, with little input from citizens or other stakeholders.



Another governance model that is prevalent in developing cities is the participatory model, where citizens and other stakeholders are actively involved in decision-making processes. This model promotes transparency and inclusivity, as it allows for the voices of different groups to be heard and considered in the decision-making process. However, this model can also be challenging to implement in practice, as it requires a high level of organization and coordination among various stakeholders.



### Subsection: 11.1b Challenges in Governance in Developing Cities



Despite the potential benefits of participatory governance, there are several challenges that hinder its effective implementation in developing cities. One of the main challenges is the lack of resources and capacity among local governments to engage in participatory processes. Many developing cities struggle with limited budgets and inadequate infrastructure, making it difficult for them to involve citizens in decision-making.



Another challenge is the unequal distribution of power and resources among different groups in society. In many developing cities, there are significant disparities in wealth and access to resources, leading to unequal representation and participation in governance processes. This can result in the voices of marginalized groups being ignored or silenced, leading to further inequalities in urban development.



### Subsection: 11.1c Strategies for Improving Governance



To address these challenges, there are several strategies that can be implemented to improve governance in developing cities. One approach is to promote capacity building among local governments, providing them with the resources and skills necessary to engage in participatory processes effectively. This can include training programs, technical assistance, and partnerships with other organizations.



Another strategy is to promote decentralization and devolution of power to local governments. This can help to address the unequal distribution of power and resources, allowing for more inclusive and equitable decision-making processes. Additionally, promoting transparency and accountability in governance can help to build trust between citizens and governments, leading to more effective and responsive decision-making.



### Conclusion



In conclusion, governance plays a crucial role in the urbanization and development of cities, especially in developing cities. Understanding the different governance models and structures that exist in these cities is essential for addressing the challenges and opportunities that arise in governing them. By promoting participatory processes, addressing challenges, and implementing effective strategies, we can improve governance in developing cities and create more inclusive and sustainable urban development.





### Section: 11.2 Role of Local Actors in Urbanization and Development:



Local actors play a crucial role in the urbanization and development of cities, especially in developing cities where rapid growth and change are occurring. In this section, we will explore the various local actors and their impact on urbanization and development.



#### 11.2a Role of Local Government



Local government is a key actor in the governance of developing cities. In Australia, local governments are responsible for providing essential services such as roads, libraries, parks, waste disposal, and town planning. They are also responsible for managing community facilities and services, including child care, tourism, and urban renewal.



The role of local government in Australia has evolved over time. In the first half of the 20th century, their main responsibility was the provision of physical infrastructure. However, from the 1970s onwards, the emphasis shifted towards community facilities and services, as well as maintenance of local roads and town planning. This change was driven by the increasing expectations of the community and the devolution of activities from higher levels of government.



One of the key sources of funding for local governments in Australia is through the collection of local land taxes, also known as "rates." They also receive grants from state and Commonwealth governments to support their services and projects. However, the distribution of resources is not equal among all local governments, with those in larger cities having access to more resources due to their larger population base.



In recent years, there has been a trend towards devolving additional powers onto local governments in Australia. This includes the power to independently enact their own local subsidiary legislation, giving them more autonomy in decision-making processes. This shift towards decentralization has been seen as a move towards "services to people" rather than just "services to property."



The role of local government in urbanization and development is crucial as they are responsible for managing the physical and social infrastructure of cities. They also play a significant role in promoting community participation and transparent management practices, which are essential for sustainable and inclusive development. However, challenges such as limited resources and competing interests among different stakeholders can make governing developing cities a complex and dynamic process. 





### Section: 11.2 Role of Local Actors in Urbanization and Development:



Local actors play a crucial role in the urbanization and development of cities, especially in developing cities where rapid growth and change are occurring. In this section, we will explore the various local actors and their impact on urbanization and development.



#### 11.2a Role of Local Government



Local government is a key actor in the governance of developing cities. #### 11.2b Role of Community Organizations



Community organizations also play a significant role in urbanization and development in developing cities. These organizations are formed by members of the community to address specific needs or objectives within their local area. They can range from small, informal groups to larger, more structured organizations.



The United Nations defines community organization as a process by which a community identifies its needs or objectives, orders them, develops the confidence and will to work towards them, and finds the resources to take action. This definition highlights the importance of community involvement and empowerment in the process of community organization.



Community organizations can have a significant impact on urbanization and development in developing cities. They often work closely with local governments and other stakeholders to identify and address community needs. They can also play a role in advocating for their community and influencing decision-making processes.



In addition to addressing immediate needs, community organizations also contribute to the long-term development of their cities. By fostering collaboration and cooperation within the community, they can help build a strong foundation for sustainable development.



However, community organizations also face challenges in their role in urbanization and development. Limited resources and funding can hinder their ability to effectively address community needs. Additionally, there may be power imbalances within the community that can affect the effectiveness of these organizations.



Despite these challenges, community organizations remain an important local actor in the governance of developing cities. Their involvement and collaboration with other stakeholders can lead to more inclusive and sustainable development. 





### Section: 11.2 Role of Local Actors in Urbanization and Development:



Local actors play a crucial role in the urbanization and development of cities, especially in developing cities where rapid growth and change are occurring. In this section, we will explore the various local actors and their impact on urbanization and development.



#### 11.2a Role of Local Government



Local government is a key actor in the governance of developing cities. In Australia, local governments are responsible for providing essential services such as roads, libraries, parks, waste disposal, and town planning. They are also responsible for managing community facilities and services, including child care, tourism, and urban renewal.



The role of local government in Australia has evolved over time. In the first half of the 20th century, their main responsibility was the provision of physical infrastructure. However, from the 1970s onwards, the emphasis shifted towards community facilities and services, as well as maintenance of local roads and town planning. This change was driven by the increasing expectations of the community and the devolution of activities from higher levels of government.



One of the key sources of funding for local governments in Australia is through the collection of local land taxes, also known as "rates." They also receive grants from state and Commonwealth governments to support their services and projects. However, the distribution of resources is not equal among all local governments, with those in larger cities having access to more resources due to their larger population base.



In recent years, there has been a trend towards devolving additional powers onto local governments in Australia. This includes the power to independently enact their own local subsidiary legislation, giving them more autonomy in decision-making processes. This shift towards decentralization has been seen as a move towards "services to people" rather than just "services to property."



#### 11.2b Role of Civil Society



Civil society, which includes non-governmental organizations (NGOs), community-based organizations (CBOs), and grassroots movements, also plays a significant role in urbanization and development. These organizations often work alongside local governments to address issues and provide services to the community.



In developing cities, civil society organizations often fill the gaps left by inadequate government services. For example, NGOs may provide education and healthcare services to underserved communities, while CBOs may work on community development projects such as building schools or improving infrastructure.



Civil society also plays a crucial role in advocating for the rights and needs of marginalized groups in developing cities. They often act as a voice for these communities and work towards creating more inclusive and equitable urban spaces.



#### 11.2c Role of Private Sector



The private sector also plays a significant role in urbanization and development in developing cities. The private sector is the part of the economy that is owned by private groups, usually for profit. In developing cities, the private sector is often the driving force behind economic growth and job creation.



In the past, the private sector has been criticized for its negative effects on urbanization and development. For example, multinational corporations may exploit cheap labor in developing cities, leading to poor working conditions and low wages for workers. However, there has been a shift towards more socially responsible practices in recent years, with some businesses choosing to self-regulate and adhere to higher standards for their workers and the environment.



The private sector also plays a role in urban planning and development. In some cases, private developers may work with local governments to build infrastructure and housing projects. However, this can also lead to issues such as gentrification and displacement of low-income communities.



In conclusion, local actors, including local government, civil society, and the private sector, all play crucial roles in urbanization and development in developing cities. It is essential for these actors to work together and collaborate to create sustainable and inclusive urban spaces for all members of the community. 





### Section: 11.3 Challenges and Opportunities in Local Governance:



Local governance plays a crucial role in the development of cities, especially in developing cities where rapid growth and change are occurring. In this section, we will explore the various challenges and opportunities faced by local governance in developing cities.



#### 11.3a Economic Challenges and Opportunities



Economic development is a key aspect of urbanization and is often seen as a measure of a city's success. However, developing cities face unique economic challenges and opportunities that can greatly impact their growth and development.



One of the main economic challenges faced by developing cities is the tradeoff between economic security and economic opportunity. This is a common issue in many developing countries, where governments must balance the need for economic stability with the desire for economic growth and development. This tradeoff can often lead to difficult decisions and policies that may not always benefit all members of society.



Another economic challenge faced by developing cities is the lack of resources and infrastructure. Many developing cities lack the necessary resources and infrastructure to support economic growth and development. This can include inadequate transportation systems, limited access to education and healthcare, and a lack of basic services such as clean water and sanitation. These challenges can hinder economic growth and make it difficult for cities to attract investment and businesses.



Despite these challenges, there are also many economic opportunities for developing cities. One of the main opportunities is the potential for rapid economic growth. Developing cities often have a large and growing population, which can create a high demand for goods and services. This can attract businesses and investment, leading to economic growth and development.



Another opportunity for developing cities is the potential for international trade and investment. Many developing countries are part of international organizations such as VISTA (Vietnam, Indonesia, South Africa, Turkey, and Argentina), which can provide access to global markets and resources. This can help boost economic growth and development in these cities.



However, along with these opportunities come challenges. One of the main challenges faced by developing cities in terms of international trade and investment is the growing levels of debt. Many developing countries have seen a rise in their debt-to-GDP ratios, which can make it difficult to attract investment and can lead to economic instability.



In addition to economic challenges and opportunities, there are also social and political challenges that can impact the development of cities. These challenges can include inappropriate or inadequate government responses, economic inequality, and high levels of poverty and unemployment.



For example, Argentina has historically experienced economic turmoil, with policies that have defied basic principles of good economic management. This has hindered the country's economic growth and development, leading to social and political challenges.



Similarly, South Africa has faced setbacks in its development due to high levels of poverty and unemployment. Despite efforts to reduce poverty since 1994, over half of the population still lives in poverty, and the country's Gini coefficient is an indication of its economic inequality.



Indonesia, on the other hand, has a resilient economy but still faces challenges in becoming a global economic power. The country has fewer global firms compared to its Asian counterparts, and its overseas direct investment holdings are half of Malaysia's. The IMF and World Bank have identified two primary issues that require government intervention - protection and support of financial regulators and weak creditor rights.



In conclusion, developing cities face a unique set of economic challenges and opportunities that can greatly impact their growth and development. It is crucial for local governance to address these challenges and take advantage of opportunities to ensure sustainable and inclusive economic growth and development. 





### Section: 11.3 Challenges and Opportunities in Local Governance:



Local governance plays a crucial role in the development of cities, especially in developing cities where rapid growth and change are occurring. In this section, we will explore the various challenges and opportunities faced by local governance in developing cities.



#### 11.3b Social Challenges and Opportunities



In addition to economic challenges and opportunities, developing cities also face significant social challenges and opportunities in local governance. These challenges and opportunities are closely intertwined with economic factors and can greatly impact the overall development of a city.



One of the main social challenges faced by developing cities is the issue of inequality. As cities grow and develop, there is often a widening gap between the rich and the poor. This can lead to social unrest and instability, as well as hinder the overall progress of the city. Local governance must address this issue by implementing policies and programs that promote social equity and provide opportunities for all members of society.



Another social challenge faced by developing cities is the issue of social cohesion. As cities become more diverse and heterogeneous, it can be difficult to maintain a sense of community and unity. This can lead to social fragmentation and hinder the ability of local governance to effectively address the needs of the city. To overcome this challenge, local governance must promote inclusivity and foster a sense of belonging among all members of society.



Despite these challenges, there are also many social opportunities for developing cities. One of the main opportunities is the potential for social innovation and collaboration. As cities face complex challenges, there is a growing need for innovative solutions that involve collaboration between different stakeholders. Local governance can play a crucial role in facilitating this collaboration and promoting social innovation.



Another opportunity for developing cities is the potential for social empowerment. As cities develop, there is often a growing sense of civic engagement and participation among citizens. Local governance can harness this energy and empower citizens to take an active role in shaping the future of their city. This can lead to more effective and sustainable development strategies that benefit the entire community.



In conclusion, local governance in developing cities faces a range of challenges and opportunities, both economic and social. It is crucial for local governance to address these challenges and capitalize on these opportunities in order to promote sustainable and inclusive development in the city. By working together with various stakeholders and promoting social equity and innovation, local governance can play a key role in shaping the future of developing cities.





### Section: 11.3 Challenges and Opportunities in Local Governance:



Local governance plays a crucial role in the development of cities, especially in developing cities where rapid growth and change are occurring. In this section, we will explore the various challenges and opportunities faced by local governance in developing cities.



#### 11.3c Environmental Challenges and Opportunities



In recent years, the issue of environmental sustainability has become a major concern for cities around the world. Developing cities, in particular, face unique challenges and opportunities in terms of environmental governance.



One of the main environmental challenges faced by developing cities is the issue of waste management. As cities grow and populations increase, the amount of waste produced also increases. This can lead to pollution, health hazards, and strain on resources. Local governance must address this issue by implementing effective waste management systems and promoting recycling and sustainable practices.



Another environmental challenge faced by developing cities is the impact of urbanization on natural resources. As cities expand, they often encroach on surrounding natural areas, leading to deforestation, loss of biodiversity, and disruption of ecosystems. Local governance must balance the need for development with the preservation of natural resources by implementing sustainable land use policies and promoting conservation efforts.



Despite these challenges, there are also many environmental opportunities for developing cities. One of the main opportunities is the potential for green infrastructure and sustainable development. As cities face the effects of climate change, there is a growing need for resilient and sustainable infrastructure. Local governance can play a crucial role in promoting and implementing green initiatives such as renewable energy, green spaces, and sustainable transportation.



In addition to these challenges and opportunities, local governance in developing cities also faces the challenge of balancing economic growth with environmental sustainability. This requires a holistic approach that takes into account the social, economic, and environmental aspects of development. Local governance must work closely with stakeholders and community members to find solutions that promote sustainable development and address the needs of the city.



In conclusion, local governance in developing cities faces a range of challenges and opportunities in terms of environmental governance. By addressing these challenges and taking advantage of opportunities, local governance can play a crucial role in promoting sustainable development and creating a better future for all members of society.





### Conclusion

In this chapter, we have explored the complex relationship between urbanization and development in developing cities. We have seen how the structure and agency of local governance play a crucial role in shaping the trajectory of urban development. From examining the historical context of urbanization to analyzing the current challenges faced by developing cities, we have gained a deeper understanding of the factors that contribute to the development of these cities.



We have seen how the structure of local governance, including the distribution of power and resources, can either facilitate or hinder the development of a city. The agency of local governments, in terms of their policies and actions, also plays a significant role in shaping the development of a city. By understanding the interplay between structure and agency, we can better comprehend the complexities of urban development in developing cities.



Furthermore, we have also explored the role of various stakeholders, such as community organizations and NGOs, in local governance. These actors can act as agents of change and contribute to the development of their cities. By empowering these stakeholders and promoting their participation in decision-making processes, local governments can foster more inclusive and sustainable development.



In conclusion, the relationship between urbanization and development in developing cities is a complex and dynamic one. By understanding the role of structure and agency in local governance, we can gain valuable insights into the challenges and opportunities faced by these cities. It is crucial for local governments to adopt inclusive and participatory approaches to governance in order to promote sustainable and equitable development in developing cities.

## Chapter: Understanding Urbanization and Development in Past and Present



### Introduction



Urbanization and development have been ongoing processes throughout human history, shaping the way we live, work, and interact with our surroundings. As our world becomes increasingly interconnected, the impact of urbanization and development has become more pronounced, with both positive and negative consequences. In this chapter, we will explore the glocal politics of urban development, examining the ways in which local and global forces intersect to shape the growth and evolution of cities. We will delve into the complexities of this dynamic relationship, exploring the harmony and havoc that can result from the interplay between local and global forces in urban development. By understanding the historical and contemporary context of urbanization and development, we can gain valuable insights into the challenges and opportunities that lie ahead for our cities.





# Understanding Urbanization and Development in Past and Present



## Chapter 12: The Glocal Politics of Urban Development: Harmony and Havoc



### Section: 12.1 Global and Local Dynamics in Urban Development



In this section, we will explore the complex relationship between global and local forces in urban development. As our world becomes increasingly interconnected, the impact of globalization on urbanization and development has become more pronounced. Globalization, defined as the process of increasing interconnectedness and interdependence among countries, has had a significant impact on the growth and evolution of cities.



#### 12.1a Role of Globalization



Globalization has been a driving force behind the rapid urbanization and development of cities around the world. The increased flow of goods, capital, and people across borders has led to the growth of cities as hubs for trade, commerce, and innovation. This has resulted in the concentration of economic activity and opportunities in urban areas, leading to the rise of megacities and the expansion of existing cities.



However, the impact of globalization on urban development is not always positive. The influx of global capital and investment can lead to gentrification and displacement of local communities. The rise of global corporations and the homogenization of culture can also threaten the unique identity and character of cities.



### Related Context



Globalization has been a topic of debate and discussion in recent years. Some argue that it has led to increased economic growth and development, while others argue that it has widened the gap between the rich and the poor. Kiani and Schofield (year) argue that the impact of globalization on urban development is not as straightforward as it may seem. They suggest that the concept of "governance" is crucial in understanding the relationship between global and local forces in urban development.



Governance refers to the ways in which nation states and international bodies interact and collaborate in managing global economic, political, and cultural relationships. Kiani and Schofield argue that effective governance can mitigate the negative effects of globalization on urban development, while also allowing for the creation of national strategies for international control.



### Last textbook section content:



Urbanization and development have been ongoing processes throughout human history, shaping the way we live, work, and interact with our surroundings. As our world becomes increasingly interconnected, the impact of urbanization and development has become more pronounced, with both positive and negative consequences. In this chapter, we will explore the glocal politics of urban development, examining the ways in which local and global forces intersect to shape the growth and evolution of cities. We will delve into the complexities of this dynamic relationship, exploring the harmony and havoc that can result from the interplay between local and global forces in urban development. By understanding the historical and contemporary context of urbanization and development, we can gain valuable insights into the challenges and opportunities that lie ahead for our cities.





# Understanding Urbanization and Development in Past and Present



## Chapter 12: The Glocal Politics of Urban Development: Harmony and Havoc



### Section: 12.1 Global and Local Dynamics in Urban Development



In this section, we will explore the complex relationship between global and local forces in urban development. As our world becomes increasingly interconnected, the impact of globalization on urbanization and development has become more pronounced. Globalization, defined as the process of increasing interconnectedness and interdependence among countries, has had a significant impact on the growth and evolution of cities.



#### 12.1a Role of Globalization



Globalization has been a driving force behind the rapid urbanization and development of cities around the world. The increased flow of goods, capital, and people across borders has led to the growth of cities as hubs for trade, commerce, and innovation. This has resulted in the concentration of economic activity and opportunities in urban areas, leading to the rise of megacities and the expansion of existing cities.



However, the impact of globalization on urban development is not always positive. The influx of global capital and investment can lead to gentrification and displacement of local communities. The rise of global corporations and the homogenization of culture can also threaten the unique identity and character of cities.



### Related Context



Globalization has been a topic of debate and discussion in recent years. Some argue that it has led to increased economic growth and development, while others argue that it has widened the gap between the rich and the poor. Kiani and Schofield (year) argue that the impact of globalization on urban development is not as straightforward as it may seem. They suggest that the concept of "governance" is crucial in understanding the relationship between global and local forces in urban development.



Governance refers to the ways in which nation states and international organizations interact and make decisions that affect urban development. It is a complex and dynamic process that involves multiple actors and stakeholders, including governments, private corporations, and local communities. The role of governance in urban development is particularly important in the context of globalization, as it can either facilitate or hinder the impact of global forces on cities.



### Subsection: 12.1b Role of Local Context



While globalization has undoubtedly played a significant role in shaping urban development, the local context also plays a crucial role. Local factors such as history, culture, and politics can greatly influence the impact of global forces on cities. For example, a city with a strong sense of community and local identity may be more resistant to the homogenizing effects of globalization.



Furthermore, the role of local governments and community organizations in decision-making processes can greatly impact the outcomes of urban development. In some cases, local actors may resist or negotiate with global forces to protect the interests of their communities. This highlights the importance of considering the local context in understanding the dynamics of urban development.



### Multimodal language models



Multimodal language models, such as GPT-4, have the potential to greatly enhance our understanding of the complex relationship between global and local forces in urban development. These models can analyze and interpret large amounts of data from various sources, including text, images, and videos, to provide a comprehensive understanding of urban development processes.



By incorporating data from both global and local sources, multimodal language models can help identify patterns and trends in urban development and provide insights into the role of different actors and factors. This can aid in the development of more effective and sustainable urban development strategies that take into account both global and local dynamics.



### Localities (districts)



The concept of localities, or districts, is crucial in understanding the role of the local context in urban development. Localities refer to specific areas within a city that have distinct characteristics and identities. These can include cultural, economic, and social factors that shape the development of the area.



By studying and understanding the unique characteristics of different localities, we can gain a better understanding of how global forces interact with the local context in shaping urban development. This can help inform decision-making processes and promote more inclusive and sustainable development that takes into account the needs and interests of local communities.

### Related Context



Globalization has been a topic of debate and discussion in recent years. Some argue that it has led to increased economic growth and development, while others argue that it has widened the gap between the rich and the poor. Kiani and Schofield (year) argue that the impact of globalization on urban development is not as straightforward as it may seem. They suggest that the concept of "governance" is crucial in understanding the relationship between global and local forces in urban development.



Governance refers to the ways in which nation states and international organizations interact and make decisions that affect the development of cities. It is a complex and dynamic process that involves multiple actors, including governments, private corporations, and civil society organizations. The role of governance in balancing global and local dynamics in urban development is crucial.



#### 12.1b Strategies for Balancing Global and Local Dynamics



In order to achieve a harmonious balance between global and local forces in urban development, it is important to consider strategies that promote inclusive and sustainable growth. One approach is to prioritize local community involvement and participation in decision-making processes. This can help ensure that the needs and concerns of local residents are taken into account when making development plans.



Another strategy is to promote responsible and ethical practices among global corporations and investors. This can help mitigate the negative impacts of globalization on local communities and ensure that development is sustainable and beneficial for all stakeholders.



Furthermore, governments can play a crucial role in regulating and managing the flow of global capital and investment into cities. This can help prevent the negative effects of gentrification and displacement, while also promoting equitable and inclusive development.



### Conclusion



In conclusion, the relationship between global and local forces in urban development is complex and multifaceted. While globalization has played a significant role in the growth and evolution of cities, it is important to consider strategies for balancing these forces in order to achieve sustainable and inclusive development. By prioritizing local community involvement, promoting responsible practices among global actors, and implementing effective governance, we can create a more harmonious and equitable urban landscape for all.





# Understanding Urbanization and Development in Past and Present



## Chapter 12: The Glocal Politics of Urban Development: Harmony and Havoc



### Section: 12.2 Conflicts and Tensions in Urban Development Processes



In this section, we will examine the various conflicts and tensions that arise in the process of urban development. As cities continue to grow and evolve, they face a multitude of challenges and competing interests that can lead to conflicts and tensions between different stakeholders.



#### 12.2a Economic Conflicts and Tensions



One of the main sources of conflict in urban development is economic inequality. As mentioned in the previous section, globalization has led to the concentration of economic activity and opportunities in urban areas. This has resulted in the growth of megacities and the expansion of existing cities, but it has also widened the gap between the rich and the poor.



The tradeoff between economic security and economic opportunity is a key factor in this conflict. While economic growth and development can bring about opportunities for some, it can also lead to displacement and gentrification for others. This can create tensions between different social classes and communities within a city.



Furthermore, the recent global energy crisis and inflation surge have also exacerbated economic conflicts and tensions. The 2021-2022 global energy crisis has led to an increase in energy prices, affecting the cost of living for many individuals and businesses. This, coupled with the 2021-2022 inflation surge, has put a strain on the economic security of many people, particularly those in low-income communities.



In addition to economic conflicts within a city, there are also tensions between different countries and their economic interests. The unequal distribution of wealth and resources among nations has led to unequal peace, where the motives for conflict are no longer concentrated among the powerful, but among the poor and between the poor and the rich. This has led to armed conflicts and development traps in around 60 countries.



The Russo-Ukrainian War in 2022 is a prime example of how economic interests can lead to conflicts between nations. The Russian invasion of Ukraine was driven by economic and political motives, causing tensions between the two countries and their allies.



### Related Context



The impact of economic inequality on conflict and development has been a topic of debate in recent years. Some argue that inequality is a potential source of internal conflict, while others argue that the evidence surrounding this relationship remains inconclusive. However, studies have shown that states with the most dissimilar interests are more likely to experience conflict, depending on external determinants such as uncertainty about the balance of power and opponent's resolve.



In addition, the concept of "governance" is crucial in understanding the relationship between economic conflicts and tensions in urban development. Kiani and Schofield (year) argue that effective governance is necessary to address economic inequality and promote peace and stability in cities. This includes addressing issues such as unequal distribution of resources and promoting democratic interests, which can help reduce conflicts and tensions in the long run.





# Understanding Urbanization and Development in Past and Present



## Chapter 12: The Glocal Politics of Urban Development: Harmony and Havoc



### Section: 12.2 Conflicts and Tensions in Urban Development Processes



In this section, we will explore the various conflicts and tensions that arise in the process of urban development. As cities continue to grow and evolve, they face a multitude of challenges and competing interests that can lead to conflicts and tensions between different stakeholders.



#### 12.2b Social Conflicts and Tensions



In addition to economic conflicts, social conflicts and tensions also play a significant role in urban development processes. These conflicts arise from the unequal distribution of resources and opportunities among different social groups within a city.



One of the main sources of social conflict is the denial of basic human needs to a large portion of the population. This can lead to instances of protracted social violence, as argued by Azar. Four preconditions are identified by Azar as the predominant sources of protracted social conflict: communal content, deprivation of human needs, governance and the state's role, and international linkages.



The first precondition, communal content, refers to the creation of identity groups within a society. This can lead to a disconnection between the state and society, as individuals turn to their social groups for stability and support. This disconnection can be traced back to the colonial legacy, where European ideas of territorial statehood were imposed on communal groups, resulting in the domination of certain identity groups over others.



The second precondition, deprivation of human needs, is closely linked to economic conflicts. As economic opportunities and resources are concentrated in urban areas, those living in poverty are often denied access to basic necessities. This can create tensions between different social classes and communities within a city.



Furthermore, the recent global energy crisis and inflation surge have also exacerbated social conflicts and tensions. The unequal distribution of wealth and resources among nations has led to unequal peace, where the motives for conflict are no longer concentrated among the powerful, but among the poor and between the poor and the rich.



To overcome these social conflicts and tensions, it is crucial to stress national identity over individual group identity. This can help bridge the gap between different social groups and promote a sense of unity and cooperation within a city. Additionally, addressing economic inequality and ensuring access to basic human needs can also help alleviate social tensions and promote harmony in urban development processes.





# Understanding Urbanization and Development in Past and Present



## Chapter 12: The Glocal Politics of Urban Development: Harmony and Havoc



### Section: 12.2 Conflicts and Tensions in Urban Development Processes



In this section, we will delve into the various conflicts and tensions that arise in the process of urban development. As cities continue to grow and evolve, they face a multitude of challenges and competing interests that can lead to conflicts and tensions between different stakeholders.



#### 12.2c Environmental Conflicts and Tensions



In recent years, there has been a growing recognition of the impact of urban development on the environment. This has led to an increase in environmental conflicts and tensions, as different actors vie for control over natural resources and grapple with the consequences of pollution and climate change.



One type of environmental conflict is known as Ecological Distribution Conflicts (EDCs). These conflicts arise from the unequal access to natural resources and the unequal distribution of the burdens of environmental pollution. For example, a factory may pollute a river, affecting the livelihoods of the community that depends on the water. Similarly, the effects of the climate crisis, such as sea level rise, disproportionately impact certain communities and are often not adequately compensated.



EDCs occur at both global and local scales. Often, conflicts arise between the global North and global South, as seen in the case of a Finnish forest company operating in Indonesia. However, there is also a growing emergence of conflicts in Europe, including violent ones. Additionally, there are local conflicts that occur within a short commodity chain, such as the extraction of sand and gravel for a nearby cement factory.



The concept of Ecological Distribution Conflicts has its roots in political ecology, ecological economics, and ecofeminism. It has also been adopted by the environmental justice movement, which seeks to bridge academia and activism to support social movements in legal struggles.



The prevalence of EDCs can be traced back to the economic system of capitalism. In his 1874 lecture 'Wage Labour and Capital', Karl Marx introduced the idea that capitalism is inherently exploitative, leading to economic inequality. This is because capitalism requires constant expansion, which often comes at the expense of marginalized communities.



In addition to economic factors, social conflicts and tensions also play a significant role in environmental conflicts. The unequal distribution of resources and opportunities among different social groups within a city can lead to tensions and violence. This is often exacerbated by the colonial legacy, where European ideas of territorial statehood were imposed on communal groups, resulting in the domination of certain identity groups over others.



In conclusion, environmental conflicts and tensions are a significant aspect of urban development processes. As cities continue to grow and evolve, it is crucial to address these conflicts and work towards sustainable and equitable development for all stakeholders. 





# Understanding Urbanization and Development in Past and Present



## Chapter 12: The Glocal Politics of Urban Development: Harmony and Havoc



### Section: 12.3 Strategies for Promoting Harmonious Urban Development



In order to address the conflicts and tensions that arise in the process of urban development, it is crucial to have effective strategies in place. These strategies should aim to promote harmonious urban development, where the needs and interests of all stakeholders are taken into consideration.



#### 12.3a Role of Urban Planning



Urban planning plays a crucial role in promoting harmonious urban development. As mentioned in the previous section, urban planners are responsible for considering urban planning at a macro scale, taking into account the needs and interests of the entire city or region.



One key aspect of urban planning is regional planning. This involves planning for land use, infrastructure, and settlement growth over a geographical area that extends beyond the local neighborhood level. By considering the needs and interests of the entire region, urban planners can help to prevent conflicts and tensions that may arise from competing interests within a specific locality.



Another important aspect of urban planning is heritage and conservation. Urban planners are responsible for identifying, protecting, and conserving buildings and places that hold cultural heritage significance. This not only helps to preserve the history and character of a city, but it also involves engaging with the community and considering their input and concerns. By involving the community in the planning process, urban planners can promote a sense of ownership and pride in the development of their city.



Urban revitalization is another key strategy for promoting harmonious urban development. As cities continue to grow and evolve, certain areas may decline and require redevelopment. Urban planners are responsible for preparing plans for the revitalization of these areas, which often involve obtaining funding from government sources. By carefully considering the needs and interests of all stakeholders, including government agencies, landowners, and community groups, urban planners can help to ensure that the revitalization process is inclusive and beneficial for all.



Master planning is also an important tool for promoting harmonious urban development. This involves planning for the ultimate spatial layout of land uses in a greenfield development project. By carefully considering the needs and interests of all stakeholders, including developers, residents, and local businesses, urban planners can help to create a cohesive and sustainable development that benefits the entire community.



In conclusion, the role of urban planning is crucial in promoting harmonious urban development. By considering the needs and interests of all stakeholders and engaging with the community, urban planners can help to prevent conflicts and tensions and create a more inclusive and sustainable city. 





# Understanding Urbanization and Development in Past and Present



## Chapter 12: The Glocal Politics of Urban Development: Harmony and Havoc



### Section: 12.3 Strategies for Promoting Harmonious Urban Development



In order to address the conflicts and tensions that arise in the process of urban development, it is crucial to have effective strategies in place. These strategies should aim to promote harmonious urban development, where the needs and interests of all stakeholders are taken into consideration.



#### 12.3b Role of Community Engagement



Community engagement plays a vital role in promoting harmonious urban development. By involving the community in the planning and decision-making process, their needs and concerns can be addressed, leading to a more inclusive and collaborative approach to urban development.



One of the key benefits of community engagement is fostering a sense of ownership and pride in the development of the city. When community members are actively involved in the planning process, they are more likely to feel invested in the outcome and take pride in their city's development. This can lead to a stronger sense of community and a more harmonious relationship between residents and local government.



However, there are also challenges to consider when it comes to community engagement. Distrust, role clarification, and time constraints can all hinder effective community engagement. It is important for urban planners to address these challenges and find ways to overcome them in order to promote successful community engagement.



One way to promote community engagement is through community collaboration. This involves creating democratic spaces where community members can openly discuss their concerns and work towards finding solutions for issues that affect the public interest. These spaces can include neighborhood associations, school boards, and resource centers where citizens can obtain information about their community and participate in decision-making processes.



Colleges and universities also play a role in promoting community engagement. Many institutions are now offering opportunities for students to engage in community volunteer work, which not only benefits the community but also helps to develop civic leadership skills in students. A case study conducted in a US college in 2014 found that active, adaptive, and resilient leadership, as well as learning for leadership and engagement for the greater good, were key factors in the success of a national initiative called The Democracy Commitment (TDC). This initiative aims to educate community college students for democracy and promote civic engagement.



In conclusion, community engagement is a crucial strategy for promoting harmonious urban development. By involving the community in the planning and decision-making process, urban planners can address the needs and concerns of all stakeholders and foster a sense of ownership and pride in the development of their city. However, it is important to address challenges and find ways to overcome them in order to ensure successful community engagement.





# Understanding Urbanization and Development in Past and Present



## Chapter 12: The Glocal Politics of Urban Development: Harmony and Havoc



### Section: 12.3 Strategies for Promoting Harmonious Urban Development



In order to address the conflicts and tensions that arise in the process of urban development, it is crucial to have effective strategies in place. These strategies should aim to promote harmonious urban development, where the needs and interests of all stakeholders are taken into consideration.



#### 12.3c Role of Conflict Resolution



Conflict resolution plays a crucial role in promoting harmonious urban development. It involves finding peaceful and mutually beneficial solutions to conflicts that arise between different stakeholders in the urban development process. In this subsection, we will discuss the role of conflict resolution in promoting harmonious urban development.



One approach to conflict resolution that has been specifically designed to mitigate protracted social conflict is the ARIA model, developed by Rothman. This model focuses on addressing identity issues, which are often at the core of conflicts. By addressing these underlying identity needs, the ARIA model aims to break down barriers and promote understanding between conflicting parties.



The ARIA model consists of four phases: antagonism, resonance, insight, and action. In the first phase, antagonism, the focus is on the tangible "what" of the conflict. This involves identifying and articulating the underlying values and needs of each party. By bringing these animosities to the forefront, it is hoped that the mutual benefits of ending the conflict can be realized.



The second phase, resonance, involves examining the "why" and "who" of the conflict. This is where the identity needs of all sides are brought to the forefront, with the goal of moving from positional bargaining to interest-based approaches. This phase involves deep dialogue and giving a voice to the underlying needs of the various parties.



The third phase, insight, focuses on finding common ground and understanding between conflicting parties. This involves exploring the underlying causes of the conflict and finding ways to address them. By promoting understanding and empathy, this phase aims to build a foundation for a mutually beneficial resolution.



The final phase, action, involves implementing the agreed-upon solutions and monitoring their effectiveness. This phase also includes building mechanisms for ongoing communication and conflict resolution to prevent future conflicts.



In addition to the ARIA model, there are other strategies for promoting harmonious urban development through conflict resolution. These include mediation, negotiation, and community collaboration. Mediation involves a neutral third party facilitating communication and finding a mutually acceptable solution. Negotiation involves direct communication between conflicting parties to find a compromise. Community collaboration involves creating democratic spaces for community members to openly discuss their concerns and work towards solutions.



In conclusion, conflict resolution plays a crucial role in promoting harmonious urban development. By addressing underlying identity issues and promoting understanding and empathy between conflicting parties, conflicts can be resolved in a peaceful and mutually beneficial manner. The ARIA model and other strategies can be effective tools in achieving this goal. 





### Conclusion

In this chapter, we have explored the complex and ever-evolving relationship between urbanization and development. We have seen how the concept of 'glocal' politics, which refers to the interplay between global and local forces, has shaped the development of cities throughout history. From the ancient civilizations of Mesopotamia to the modern metropolises of today, urban development has been influenced by a variety of factors such as economic, social, and political forces.



One of the key takeaways from this chapter is the importance of finding a balance between harmony and havoc in urban development. On one hand, cities need to strive for harmony by promoting sustainable and inclusive growth, ensuring the well-being of their citizens, and preserving their cultural heritage. On the other hand, cities also need to be prepared for the havoc that can arise from rapid urbanization, such as environmental degradation, social inequality, and political instability.



As we move forward, it is crucial to continue studying and understanding the complexities of urbanization and development. By learning from the successes and failures of past and present cities, we can work towards creating more livable, resilient, and equitable urban spaces for future generations.
